<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1092331828">@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .contains-special-characters{width:22em}}</style><div class="side-box metadata side-box-right contains-special-characters noprint selfref"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Bali_Ba.png/40px-Bali_Ba.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Bali_Ba.png/60px-Bali_Ba.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Bali_Ba.png/80px-Bali_Ba.png 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="864" /></span></span></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Balinese_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Balinese alphabet">Balinese alphabet</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support#Balinese" title="Help:Multilingual support">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a>&#32;instead of Balinese characters.</div></div>
</div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm/250px--WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="250" height="188" data-durationhint="90" data-mwtitle="WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-width="640" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/77/WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm/WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm.m3u8" type="application/vnd.apple.mpegurl" data-transcodekey="m3u8" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/77/WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm/WIKITONGUES_-_Ni_Luh_speaking_Balinese.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="480" data-height="360" /></video></span><figcaption>Balinese language speaker</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Balinese</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian_languages" title="Malayo-Polynesian languages">Malayo-Polynesian language</a> spoken by 3.3&#160;million people (as of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>) on the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a>, as well as Northern <a href="/wiki/Nusa_Penida" title="Nusa Penida">Nusa Penida</a>, Western <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a>, Eastern <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Southern <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sulawesi" title="Sulawesi">Sulawesi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Clynes_1995_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clynes_1995-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Most Balinese speakers also use <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>. The Bali Cultural Agency estimated in 2011 that the number of people still using the Balinese language in their daily lives on the <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> Island is under 1&#160;million. The language has been classified as "not endangered" by <i><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The higher <a href="/wiki/Register_(sociolinguistics)" title="Register (sociolinguistics)">registers</a> of the language borrow extensively from <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a>: an old form of classical Javanese, <a href="/wiki/Kawi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kawi language">Kawi</a>, is used in Bali as a <a href="/wiki/Liturgical_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Liturgical language">religious</a> and ceremonial language.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Balinese is an <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian language">Austronesian language</a> belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian_languages" title="Malayo-Polynesian languages">Malayo-Polynesian branch</a> of the family. Within Malayo-Polynesian, it is part of the <a href="/wiki/Bali%E2%80%93Sasak%E2%80%93Sumbawa_languages" title="Bali–Sasak–Sumbawa languages">Bali–Sasak–Sumbawa</a> subgroup.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Internally, Balinese has three distinct varieties; Highland Bali, Lowland Bali, and Nusa Penida.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the 2000 census, the Balinese language is spoken by 3.3&#160;million people in Indonesia, mainly concentrated on the island of Bali and the surrounding areas.
</p><p>In 2011, the Bali Cultural Agency estimated that the number of people still using the Balinese language in their daily lives on <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> Island does not exceed 1&#160;million, as in urban areas their parents only introduce the <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian language</a> or even English as a foreign language, while daily conversations in the institutions and the mass media have disappeared. The written form of the Balinese language is increasingly unfamiliar and most Balinese people use the Balinese language only as a means of oral communication, often mixing it with Indonesian in their daily speech. However in the transmigration areas outside Bali Island, the Balinese language is extensively used and believed to play an important role in the survival of the language.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The official spelling denotes both <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> by <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;a&#x27e9;</span>.  However, <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;a&#x27e9;</span> is usually pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ə]</span> when it ends a word, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ə]</span> occurs also in prefixes <i>ma-</i>, <i>pa-</i> and <i>da-</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Spitzing_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spitzing-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<td style="border-left: 0;"><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_trill" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced alveolar trill">r</a></span>
</td>
<td colspan="2">
</td>
<td colspan="2">
</td>
<td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Depending on dialect, the phoneme <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span> is realized as a voiceless <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">alveolar</a> or <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_consonant" title="Retroflex consonant">retroflex</a> stop. This is in contrast with most other languages in western Indonesia (including <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Standard Indonesian</a>), which have a dental <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span> patterning with an otherwise alveolar phoneme series.<sup id="cite_ref-Clynes_1995_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clynes_1995-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress">Stress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Stress"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stress falls on the last syllable.<sup id="cite_ref-Spitzing_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spitzing-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Registers">Registers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Registers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Even though most of the basic vocabulary in Balinese and Indonesian are of Austronesian and Sanskrit origin, many cognates in both languages sound quite different.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Balinese has different <a href="/wiki/Register_(sociolinguistics)" title="Register (sociolinguistics)">registers</a> depending on the relationship and status of those speaking: low (<span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">basa ketah</i></span>), middle (<span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">basa madia</i></span>), and high (<span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">basa singgih</i></span>). <span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">Basa singgih</i></span> contains many <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> (specifically <a href="/wiki/Old_Javanese" title="Old Javanese">Old Javanese</a>) which reflect the fifteenth-century usage spoken by Old Javanese. The common mutations in inherited Balinese words are:
</p>
<ul><li>First, mutation r into h of initial r, intervocalic r, and final r</li>
<li>Second, h into ø, everywhere except the final consonant</li></ul>
<p>However, these mutations are not expressed by the High Balinese, thus this infer high Balinese was <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> and (<a href="/wiki/Old_Javanese" title="Old Javanese">Old</a>) <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a>. These loanwords are identical in sound with their Javanese cognates.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Numerals">Numerals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Numerals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Balinese_numerals" title="Balinese numerals">Balinese numerals</a></div>
<p>Balinese has a decimal numeral system, but this is complicated by numerous words for intermediate quantities such as 45, 175, and 1600.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The word order is similar to that of <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, and verb and noun <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflectional</a> <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">morphology</a> is similarly minimal.  However, <a href="/wiki/Derivation_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Derivation (linguistics)">derivational</a> morphology is extensive, and suffixes are applied to indicate definite or indefinite articles, and optionally to indicate <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">possession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Spitzing_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spitzing-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">Writing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Writing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Balinese has been written in two different <a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing systems</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Balinese_script" title="Balinese script">Balinese script</a>, and in modern times the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Balinese_script">Balinese script</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Balinese script"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanacaraka-bali.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hanacaraka-bali.svg/400px-Hanacaraka-bali.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="131" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hanacaraka-bali.svg/600px-Hanacaraka-bali.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hanacaraka-bali.svg/800px-Hanacaraka-bali.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="180" /></a><figcaption>Basic signs of the Balinese script<br /><small>Note: The script is arranged in Javanese order.</small></figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Balinese_script" title="Balinese script">Balinese script</a></div>
<p>The Balinese script (<span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">Aksara Bali</i></span>, <span title="Balinese-language text"><span lang="ban">ᬅᬓ᭄ᬱᬭᬩᬮᬶ</span></span>), which is arranged as <span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn"><a href="/wiki/Balinese_script" title="Balinese script">Hanacaraka</a></i></span> (<span title="Balinese-language text"><span lang="ban">ᬳᬦᬘᬭᬓ</span></span>), is an <a href="/wiki/Abugida" title="Abugida">abugida</a>, ultimately derived from the <a href="/wiki/Br%C4%81hm%C4%AB_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Brāhmī script">Brāhmī script</a> of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. The earliest known inscriptions date from the 9th century AD.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Few people today are familiar with the Balinese script.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Balinese script is almost the same as the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_script" title="Javanese script">Javanese script</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_alphabet">Latin alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Latin alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Schools in Bali today teach a Latin alphabet known as <span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">Tulisan Bali</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Page from a Bible printed with Balinese script"><img alt="Page from a Bible printed with Balinese script" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg/120px-Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="110" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg/180px-Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg/240px-Bible_printed_with_Balinese_script.jpg 2x" data-file-width="679" data-file-height="625" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Page from a <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> printed with Balinese script</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Note">Note</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Balinese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Note"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><small>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1041539562">.mw-parser-output .citation{word-wrap:break-word}.mw-parser-output .citation:target{background-color:rgba(0,127,255,0.133)}</style><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1"><b><a href="#ref_1">^1</a></b></span>  In Balinese script, <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kawi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kawi language">Kawi</a> loanwords tend use conservative orthography as standard form in Balinese script. The word for language, <a href="/wiki/Bahasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahasa"><i>basa</i></a>, in Balinese is a loanword from <a href="/wiki/Old_Javanese" title="Old Javanese">Old Javanese</a> <span title="Kawi-language romanization"><i lang="kaw-Latn">bhāṣa</i></span> which came from the Sanskrit word <span title="Sanskrit-language text"><span lang="sa">भाषा</span></span> <span title="Sanskrit-language romanization"><i lang="sa-Latn">bhāṣā</i></span>, hence it is written according to Sanskrit and Old Javanese spelling <span title="Balinese-language text"><span lang="ban">ᬪᬵᬱᬩᬮᬶ</span></span> in Balinese script. The <span title="Balinese-language text"><i lang="ban">Bali</i></span> form in Balinese script is used by beginner writers. Meanwhile, diacritics are not written in the current romanization of the Balinese language. Thus, both <span title="Balinese-language text"><i lang="ban">Bali</i></span> and <span title="Balinese-language romanization"><i lang="ban-Latn">basa Bali</i></span> are the standard forms.
</small>
</p>
